Definition of Motion as First Perfection
Definition of motion as first perfection with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why motion is defined as a 'first perfection' and how this definition avoids circularity while distinguishing motion from arrival and other perfections.

Core Idea
Motion is the gradual orientation toward a goal, not the arrival itself.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid presents a philosophical definition of motion that avoids circularity. The author explains why motion must be understood as a 'first perfection' for a body in potentiality, distinguishing it from the endpoint (arrival) and from other perfections like substantial form. Let's unpack this definition step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation to get a general understanding.
Pay attention to the technical terms: حركة, كمال أول, قوة, فعل.
2
Understand the problem with previous definitions
The author criticizes definitions of motion as 'gradual exit from potentiality to actuality' because they rely on time, which itself depends on motion, creating circularity.
This motivates the need for a definition that does not presuppose time.
3
Analyze the definition's components
Break down the definition: 'first perfection for that which is in potentiality insofar as it is in potentiality'. Understand each qualifier.
Focus on why 'first' and 'insofar as it is in potentiality' are crucial.
4
Distinguish motion from arrival and other perfections
Motion is the orientation toward a goal while potentiality remains; arrival is a second perfection. Unlike substantial form, motion is a perfection from the aspect of potentiality, not actuality.
This clarifies what motion is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للمتحرك، إنما هو في الوصول الذي له بالقوة فتخرج كمالاته التي ليست كذلك، كالمربعية مثلا، والمقصود تلخيص المعنى المسمى بالحركة على الإطلاق، وتحقيقه لا تمييزه (۱) وتصويره عند العقل، فلا يضيره كون المعرف أخفى، وكون الكمالين. أعني التوجه والوصول في الحركة المستديرة بمجرد الفرض والاعتبار نظراً إلى أن حال الجسم بالنسبة إلى كل نقطة من حيث طلبها توجه ومن حيث الحصول عندها وصول). و المبحث الأول منه غني عن الشرح وأما الثاني فبيانه أن بعض الفلاسفة فسر الحركة بالخروج من القوة إلى الفعل على التدريج أو يسيراً يسيراً أو لا دفعة وبنى ذلك (۲) على أن معنى هذه الألفاظ واضح عند العقل من غير احتياج إلى تصور الزمان المفتقر إلى تصور الحركة، ونظر بعضهم إلى أن معنى التدريج أن لا يكون دفعة ، ومعنى الحصول دفعة أن يكون في آن وهو طرف الزمان، وهو مقدار الحركة فيكون التعريف دورياً. ففسرها بأنها كمال أول لما هو بالقوة من حيث هو بالقوة والمراد بالكمال ههنا حصول ما لم يكن حاصلاً، ولا خفاء في أن الحركة أمر ممكن الحصول للجسم، فيكون حصولها كمالاً ، واحترز بقيد الأولية عن الوصول فإن الجسم إذا كان في مكان وهو ممكن الحصول في مكان آخر كان له إمكانان إمكان الحصول في ذلك المكان، وإمكان التوجه إليه وهما كمالان فالتوجه مقدم على الأصول فهو كمال أول والوصول كمال ثان ثم إن الحركة تفارق سائر الكمالات من حيث إنها لا حقيقة لها إلا التأدي إلى الغير والسلوك إليه، فلا بد من مطلوب ممكن الحصول، ليكون التوجه توجهاً إليه، ومن أن يبقى من ذلك التوجه ما دام موجوداً شيء بالقوة، إذ لا توجه بعد الوصول، فحقيقة الحركة متعلقة بأن يبقى منها شيء بالقوة وبأن لا يكون المتأدى إليه حاصلا بالفعل، فتكون الحركة بالفعل كمالاً للجسم المتحرك الذي هو بالقوة من جهة التأدى إلى المقصود الذي هو الحصول في المكان المطلوب فيكون كمالاً أول لما بالقوة، لكن من جهة أنه بالقوة لا جهة أنه بالفعل ولا من جهة أخرى، فإن الحركة لا تكون كمالاً للجسم في جسميته أو في شكله أو نحو ذلك، بل من الجهة التي هو باعتبارها كان بالقوة، أعني الحصول في المكان الآخر، واحترز بهذا التي ليست كذلك كالصورة النوعية (۱) فإنها كمال أول للمتحرك الذي لم يصل إلى المقصد، لكن لا من حيث هو بالقوة بل من حيث هو بالفعل .
For the moving body, it is only in the arriving that it has in potentiality, so its perfections that are not like that are excluded, such as squareness for example. And the purpose is to summarize the meaning called 'motion' absolutely, and to realize it, not to distinguish it (1) and picture it in the mind. So it does not harm it that the definiendum is more obscure, and that the two perfections—I mean the orientation and the arriving in circular motion—are merely by supposition and consideration, with respect to the fact that the state of the body relative to every point, from the perspective of its seeking, is orientation, and from the perspective of its arriving at it is arriving. And the first part of it does not need explanation. As for the second, its clarification is that some philosophers interpreted motion as the exit from potentiality to actuality gradually, or little by little, or not instantaneously, and they built that (2) on the idea that the meaning of these words is clear to the intellect without needing to conceive time, which depends on conceiving motion. And some of them considered that the meaning of 'gradual' is that it is not instantaneous, and the meaning of 'instantaneous occurring' is that it is in an instant, which is the extremity of time, which is the measure of motion; thus the definition becomes circular. So he interpreted it as: a first perfection for that which is in potentiality insofar as it is in potentiality. And what is meant by 'perfection' here is the occurrence of what was not occurring. And there is no concealment that motion is a thing possible of occurrence for the body, so its occurrence is a perfection. And he guarded by the qualifier 'first' against arrival; for if the body is in a place and it is possible for it to occur in another place, it has two potentialities: the potentiality of occurring in that place and the potentiality of orientation towards it, and they are two perfections. So orientation is prior to occurrence, so it is a first perfection, and arrival is a second perfection. Then motion differs from other perfections in that it has no reality except the leading to another and the journeying to it. So there must be a sought thing possible of occurrence, so that the orientation is an orientation towards it, and that there remains from that orientation as long as it exists something in potentiality, since there is no orientation after arrival. So the reality of motion is connected to the fact that there remains from it something in potentiality and that that which is led to is not actually occurring. So motion in actuality is a perfection for the moving body that is in potentiality, from the aspect of leading to the intended goal which is occurring in the desired place; so it is a first perfection for that which is in potentiality, but from the aspect that it is in potentiality, not from the aspect that it is in actuality, nor from another aspect. For motion is not a perfection for the body in its corporeality or in its shape or the like, but from the aspect by which it is in potentiality, namely occurring in the other place. And he guarded by this against those perfections that are not like that, such as the specific form (1); for it is a first perfection for the moving body that has not reached the destination, but not insofar as it is in potentiality, but insofar as it is in actuality.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of motion as a philosophical concept. It begins by clarifying that the aim is to summarize the meaning of motion absolutely, not to distinguish it from other things or to produce a mental image; therefore it does not matter if the definiens is more obscure than the definiendum. The author then notes that some philosophers defined motion as a gradual exit from potentiality to actuality, but this relies on an understanding of time, which itself depends on motion, making it circular. To avoid this, the definition is given as 'a first perfection for that which is in potentiality insofar as it is in potentiality.' The term 'perfection' means the acquisition of something previously absent, and motion is a perfection because it is an acquisition for the body. The qualifier 'first' excludes 'arrival' (the endpoint), since orientation towards a place is prior to actually reaching it. Motion differs from other perfections because its reality consists solely in leading to something else; thus it requires that a potentiality remains as long as motion exists, and that the goal is not yet actual. Consequently, motion is a perfection of the body from the aspect of its potentiality for reaching another place, not from the aspect of its actual corporeal attributes. Finally, the author distinguishes motion from other 'first perfections' like substantial form, which is a perfection of the body's actual nature, not its potentiality. The explanation follows the definition clause by clause, ensuring each element is justified.

Key Terms

كمال أول
قوة
فعل
تدريج

توجه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Motion is the same as arriving at a destination.
Correction: Motion is the gradual orientation while potentiality remains; arrival is a second perfection, not motion itself.

Checkpoint
According to the definition in this passage, why is motion called a 'first perfection'?
A) Because it is the first perfection a body acquires in its substance.
B) Because it consists of orientation towards a goal before arrival, which is a second perfection.
C) Because it is a perfection that occurs instantaneously.
D) Because it is the same as the specific form of the body.

Key Takeaway
Motion is a first perfection for a body in potentiality, consisting of gradual orientation toward a goal that remains partly potential, and this definition avoids circularity by not relying on time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your spiritual journey toward Allah, do you view your current acts of worship as a 'first perfection'—an orientation that still leaves you in potentiality—or do you expect to have already arrived? How does that distinction affect your patience and effort?
?
The passage says motion is a perfection only from the aspect of potentiality, not actuality. Are you content with being in a state of becoming, constantly moving toward your Lord, or do you demand immediate results and perfect actuality now? What would change if you embraced the 'first perfection' mindset?
?
If motion were defined by time, it would be circular. How often do you measure your spiritual progress by the clock or by milestones, rather than by the sincerity of your orientation? Will you commit to focusing on the direction of your heart today, even if the arrival seems distant?

Objections to the Definition of Motion and Their Answers
The author presents two objections to the definition of motion and answers them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main objections raised against defining motion as 'first perfection' and how the author answers them by clarifying the definition's purpose and applying the concept of supposition to circular motion.

Core Idea
Criticisms of motion's definition are resolved by clarifying its purpose and applying suppositional perfection.

This passage addresses two criticisms of defining motion as 'first perfection'. The first objection claims the definition is more obscure than motion itself; the second says it fails for circular motion because it lacks an actual endpoint. The author responds by explaining that the definition is not meant to be a strict definition but a summary, and that for circular motion, perfections are considered relative to each supposed point along the path. Let's explore each objection and answer in detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation, to get the overall flow of objections and answers.
Notice the structure: two objections, then an answer.
2
Identify the two objections
The first objection is about the definition being more obscure than motion itself. The second objection is that the definition does not apply to circular motion. Underline the key phrases in the text.
3
Understand the answer's main point
The answer clarifies that this is not a strict definition but a summary of the meaning of motion. It then explains that for circular motion, 'first perfection' and 'second perfection' are considered by supposition relative to each point, not as actual endpoints.
The concept of 'فرض واعتبار' (supposition and consideration) is key.
4
Reflect on the reasoning
Ask yourself why the obscurity objection is not a problem for this type of definition, and how supposition allows the definition to still hold for circular motion.
This demonstrates the flexibility of kalam reasoning in addressing objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعترض أولاً بأن ،ماهية الحركة وإن لم تكن بديهية واضحة عند العقل، لكن لا خفاء في أن ما ذكر في هذا التعريف ليس بأوضح منها بل أخفى وثانياً : بأنه لا يصدق على الحركة المستديرة إذ لا منتهى لها بالفعل، فلا يتحقق كمال أول وثان وأجيب بأن هذا ليس تعريفاً للحركة يقصد بهـا تمييزها عما عداها أو تحصيل صورتها عند العقل، بل هو تلخيص وتبيين للمعنى المسمى بالحركة أينية كانت (۲) أو غير أينية فلا يضره كون تصوره أخفى من تصور ماهية الحركة، ولا كون الكمال الأول والثاني في بعض أقسام الحركة، أعني المستديرة بمجرد الفرض والاعتبار دون الفعل والحقيقة وذلك لأن كل نقطة تفرض فحال الجسم المتحرك على الاستدارة بالنسبة إليها من حيث طلبها توجه فيكون كمالاً أول ومن حيث الحصول عندها وصول فيكون كمالاً ثانياً .
And it was objected firstly that the essence of motion, even if it is not self-evident and clear to the intellect, yet there is no concealment that what is mentioned in this definition is not clearer than it, but rather more obscure. And secondly: that it does not apply to circular motion, since it has no actual endpoint, so a first and second perfection are not realized. And it was answered that this is not a definition of motion intended to distinguish it from what is other than it or to obtain its form in the mind, but rather it is a summary and explication of the meaning called motion, whether it is linear or non-linear. So it does not harm that its conception is more obscure than the conception of the essence of motion, nor does it harm that the first and second perfection in some species of motion—namely circular motion—are merely by supposition and consideration, not actual and real; because every point that is supposed—the state of the body moving in a circle relative to it is, from the perspective of its seeking it, an orientation, so it is a first perfection, and from the perspective of arriving at it, an arrival, so it is a second perfection.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage presents two objections to the definition of motion as 'first perfection' and provides their answers. The first objection argues that the definition is not clearer than the thing defined (motion itself) but rather more obscure. The second objection states that the definition fails for circular motion because circular motion has no actual endpoint, so there cannot be a first and second perfection. The answer clarifies that this discussion is not a definition meant to distinguish motion or provide a mental picture; it is merely a summary and explanation of the meaning of motion, whether rectilinear or circular. Therefore, it does not matter if the concept is less clear than the essence of motion. As for the objection about circular motion, the answer explains that in circular motion, first and second perfections are considered relative to each individual point along the path. For each supposed point, the body's seeking it is an orientation (first perfection) and arriving at it is an arrival (second perfection), even though these are mental considerations rather than actual endpoints. Thus the definition holds in a suppositional sense.

ماهية
بديهية
تعريف
تلخيص
حركة مستديرة
كمال أول
كمال ثان
فرض واعتبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The definition of motion should be clearer than motion itself and must apply to all motions with actual endpoints.
Correction: The definition is a summary, not a strict definition; circular motion's perfections are considered by supposition, so it applies.

Checkpoint
How does the answer address the objection that the definition does not apply to circular motion?
A) It admits the definition fails and offers a different definition for circular motion.
B) It argues that circular motion is not actually motion.
C) It explains that in circular motion, first and second perfections are considered with respect to each supposed point.
D) It claims that circular motion does have an actual endpoint.

Key Takeaway
The definition of motion as 'first perfection' is a summary, not a strict definition, and it applies to circular motion through suppositional perfections.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you define your own goals, do you treat them as absolute endpoints or as relative points along a continuous journey? How does the suppositional nature of perfection in circular motion challenge or affirm your approach? Commit to re-evaluating one goal this week, seeing it as a 'first perfection' rather than a final destination.
?
The author says the definition is a summary, not a strict logical tool. In your study of Islamic creed, have you ever demanded overly precise definitions that actually obscured your understanding? Where can you accept a 'summary' explanation and still build sound conviction? Write down one area where you will practice this acceptance starting today.
?
If the definition of motion itself requires intellectual humility (it's not perfectly clear), what does that say about your ability to fully grasp divine realities like Allah's attributes? How can this lesson guard you against intellectual arrogance? Pause now and ask Allah to grant you humility in seeking knowledge.

Ibn Sina's Definition of Pulse
Ibn Sina defines pulse and its composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Avicenna's definition of pulse as composed of two movements and two pauses, and the natural philosophical reasoning behind the pause.

Core Idea
Every pulse beat is an expansion followed by a contraction, with a necessary pause in between.

Sanusi quotes Avicenna to illustrate a definition from natural philosophy. Pulse is not a single motion but a composition of two opposite movements with intervening stillness. This passage shows how classical scholars integrated medical concepts into their theological curriculum.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice that Ibn Sina defines pulse as a movement of the vessels of the spirit for the purpose of cooling.
The term 'vessels of the spirit' refers to arteries carrying vital spirit.
2
Identify the components
Identify that pulse consists of two movements: expansion (diastole) and contraction (systole). Also note the two pauses between them.
Pauses are the moments of rest after expansion and after contraction.
3
Understand the reason for pauses
Ibn Sina argues that a pause is necessary because opposite movements cannot directly follow each other without an intermediate state of rest. This is a principle of natural philosophy.
The movement reaches an actual endpoint before the opposite begins.
4
Reflect on the purpose
The ultimate purpose of pulse is to cool the vital spirit by means of breath (air). Consider how this fits into broader medical theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : ومنهم : يقول ابن سينا النبض حركة من أوعية الروح مؤلفة من انبساط و انقباض لتبريد الروح بالنسيم، والنبض إما جزئي وإما كلي ونتكلم على النبض الكلي فنقول : إن كل نبضة فهي مركبة من حركتين وسكونيين لأن كل نبض مركب من انبساط و انقباض ثم لا بد من تخلل السكون بين كل حركتين متضادتين لاستحالة اتصال الحركة بحركة أخرى بعد أن يحصل لمسافتها نهاية وطرف بالفعل وهذا مما يبين في العالم الطبيعي الخ .
He said: And among them: Ibn Sina says: Pulse is a movement of the vessels of the spirit composed of expansion and contraction to cool the spirit by breath. Pulse is either particular or general. We speak of general pulse and we say: Each pulse beat is composed of two movements and two pauses because every pulse is composed of expansion and contraction, then there must be a pause between two opposite movements because it is impossible for a movement to be directly connected to another movement after its distance has reached an actual end and limit. This is demonstrated in the natural world, etc.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from a source (likely Avicenna's Canon) defining pulse. It describes pulse as a movement of the vessels of the spirit (the vital spirit) composed of expansion (diastole) and contraction (systole) for cooling the spirit by breath. It distinguishes between particular and general pulse, then focuses on general pulse. Each pulse beat consists of two movements (expansion and contraction) and two pauses (systole and diastole have intervening rests). The reason for the pause is that it is impossible for a movement to be directly followed by an opposite movement without an intermediate state of rest, because the movement reaches an actual endpoint. This is a basic principle in natural philosophy.

Key Terms

أوعية الروح
انبساط
انقباض
نسيم
سكون
حركتين متضادتين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To move blood through the body.
B) To cool the spirit by breath.
C) To maintain heart rate.
D) To provide oxygen to organs.

Key Takeaway
Each pulse beat consists of expansion and contraction separated by pauses, serving to cool the vital spirit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The pulse beat has a necessary pause between movements. In your daily life, are you forcing yourself from one activity to another without a pause, ignoring the need for rest and reflection that Allah has embedded in creation? Will you commit to inserting a short pause of gratitude or dhikr between your tasks starting today?
?
Ibn Sina says the pulse cools the spirit by breath. What 'cools' your heart when it is heated by worldly anxieties? Do you turn to the 'breath' of remembrance of Allah (dhikr) and contemplation of His signs? If not, what will you do to change that starting tomorrow morning?
?
The opposite movements of expansion and contraction cannot be consecutive without a pause. In your character, do you try to change from a bad habit to a good one overnight without a period of transition and repentance? How can you apply the divine design of pauses to your spiritual growth?

Straight vs. Curved and Upward vs. Downward Motion
Analyzes motion classification and the special case of upward/downward.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how kalam classifies motions as straight/curved and why upward and downward are considered different even though they share the same essence.

Core Idea
Motion differs not by essence but by relational opposition that never reverses.

In this passage, the author explores the nature of motion, specifically whether straight and curved motion are fundamentally different, and whether upward and downward motions are essentially the same. Using the framework of quantity and quality, he explains the classification, and then addresses a key objection about the special case of ascending and descending motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to get the overall argument.
Pay attention to the flow from general classification to specific case.
2
Understand the straight vs. curved distinction
Notice that the author says the specific difference between straight and curved motion is not obvious. He relates it to the properties of quantity and quality.
Motion is described as straight or curved because it applies to a continuous distance.
3
Examine upward/downward and the contrariety argument
Imam al-Razi argues that upward and downward do not differ in essence but in being beginning and end, which are opposed by contrariety.
This opposition is sufficient for them to be considered different motions.
4
Consider the objection and its resolution
An objection says this could apply to any motion with a start and end. The answer is that up and down have fixed real directions that never reverse.
This distinguishes them from left-right motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاستقامة يمنة ويسرة فإن الاختلاف النوعي والاتفاق فيها مما ليس بظاهر وغاية ما يمكن في ذلك أن الحركة لما انطبقت على المسافة التي هي متصل، وقد تقرر عندهم أن المستقيم والمنحني نوعان من الكم كالاستقامة والانحناء من الكيف جعلوا الحركة أيضاً كذلك، ولهذا توصف هي أيضاً: بالاستقامة والاستدارة وهذا بخلاف الزمان المنطبق على الحركة لأنه. واحد لا يعرض له التكثر والانقطاع بالفعل، وأما في الصعود والهبوط فذكر الإمام أن الطرفين، وإن لم يختلفا بالماهية لكنهما اختلفا بالمبدأيـة والمنتهية وهما متقابلان تقابل التضاد، وهذا القدر كاف في وقوع الاختلاف بين الحركتين، ويرد عليه أن هذا جاز في كل حركة من مبدأ إلى منتهى مع الرجوع عنه إلى ذلك المبدأ، إلا أن يقال لما كان مبدأ الصعود والهبوط، ومنتهاهما في جهتين حقيقيتين لا يتبدلان أصلاً، فلا يصير العلو سفلاً أو بالعكس بخلاف سائر الجهات اعتبر ذلك، ولهذا لا يمكن اعتبار الصاعدة هابطة أو بالعكس بخلاف الحركة يمنة ويسرة.
As for straightness to the right and left, indeed specific difference and agreement in it are not apparent, and the utmost possible in that is that when motion applies to the distance which is continuous, and it is established among them that the straight and the curved are two types of quantity just as straightness and curvature are from quality, they made motion also likewise, and therefore it is also described as straightness and circularity. This is contrary to time which applies to motion because it is one, not subject to multiplicity and actual interruption. As for upward and downward, the Imam mentioned that the two extremes, although they do not differ in essence, yet they differ in being beginning and end, and they are opposed by opposition of contrariety, and this much is sufficient for the occurrence of difference between the two motions. It is objected that this would apply to every motion from a beginning to an end with return from it to that beginning, except that it may be said: since the beginning of upward and downward and their end are in two real directions that never change, so the high does not become low or vice versa, unlike other directions, that was considered. And therefore it is not possible to consider the ascending motion as descending or vice versa, unlike motion to the right and left.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage discusses the classification of motion as straight or curved and the special issue of upward versus downward motion. The author begins by noting that the specific difference or agreement in straightness to the right and left is not obvious. The best that can be said is that motion is applied to a continuous distance, and just as straight and curved are two types of quantity (like straightness and curvature in quality), motion too is described as straight or circular. Time, however, is one and not subject to multiplicity or actual interruption. Then the author turns to upward and downward motion. Imam al-Razi stated that the two endpoints (up and down) do not differ in essence but differ in being a beginning versus an end. They are opposed by contrariety, and this difference is sufficient for the two motions to be different. An objection is raised: this could apply to any motion from a beginning to an end with a return to the beginning. The answer is that the beginning and end of upward and downward are in two real directions that never change; high never becomes low, unlike other directions. Therefore one cannot consider ascending as descending, unlike motion to the right and left.

الاستدارة

الهبوط

التضاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That upward and downward motion differ in their intrinsic essence (what they are).
Correction: The passage clarifies that they share the same essence; the difference is only in being a beginning versus an end, which are opposed by contrariety.

Checkpoint
Why can ascending motion not be considered descending motion according to the author?
A) Because their beginnings and ends are in the same direction.
B) Because their beginnings and ends are in two real directions that never change.

D) Because time prevents it.

Key Takeaway
Upward and downward motions are distinguished not by their intrinsic nature but by the relational opposition of their endpoints, which remain fixed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that what appears to be an essential difference (up vs down) is only relational—a matter of beginning and end. Think of an area of your life where you have considered two options as essentially opposed (e.g., success vs failure, right vs wrong). How would viewing them merely as relational opposites (different starting points or ends) change how you navigate between them? Will you commit to re-examining one such opposition this week, asking only: 'What is the beginning and what is the end here?'
?
The source argues that some directions (up/down) are fixed and never reverse, while others (right/left) are relative. In your own life, what do you treat as an absolute, non-reversible direction (like 'toward Allah' or 'away from sin')? Have you ever confused a relative direction (like cultural preference) with an absolute one? What needs to change so that your fixed direction remains truly fixed?
?
The objection in the passage is that any motion could be seen as different by its beginning and end, but the response ties difference to the fixed nature of the direction. Reflect: when you feel 'different' from someone, is that difference based on something fixed and real (like truth and falsehood) or on mere position (like a different stage in the same journey)? How will you test which it is before the next time you judge another person?

The Opposition in Motion is Due to Its Termini
The author argues that opposition in motion is due to opposition of its termini.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why opposition between two motions is ultimately caused by the opposition of their starting and ending points, and how this distinction clarifies accidental versus essential opposition.

Core Idea
Opposition in motion comes from the ends, not the mover or the medium.

This passage systematically eliminates possible causes for why motions can be opposed—the moved object, the mover, time, and the substrate—leaving only one explanation: the termini. Understanding this reasoning is essential for grasping the author's taxonomy of motion and its implications for physics and metaphysics.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the English translation. Note how the author builds his case by eliminating alternatives.
Pay attention to the structure: rejection of four possibilities, then positive proof, then distinction of essential vs accidental.
2
Follow the elimination of alternatives
Identify each alternative the author rejects (moved object, mover, time, substrate) and the reason for rejection. The passage uses specific examples to illustrate.
The examples (fire/water upward, stone/fire by force/nature, ascent/descent) are critical.
3
Deduce the positive conclusion
After eliminating alternatives, the author concludes 'it is determined that the opposition of motion is due to the opposition of its from which and to which.' Mark this as the central claim.
The phrase 'فتعين أن يكون تضاد الحركة لتضاد ما منه وما إليه' is key.
4
Distinguish essential and accidental opposition
The author classifies opposition of termini into essential (دات) and accidental (عارض). Understand the examples: color change vs. spatial motion relative to center/periphery.
Essential opposition is intrinsic to the qualities, accidental depends on external relations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا خفاء في أن اختلاف أحوال الحركة إنما يكون لاختلاف متعلقاتها، فتضاد الحركة ليس لتضاد المتحرك لأنه جسم، ولا تضاد فيه بالذات، ولو اعتبرنا التضاد بالعرض فقد يكون متضاداً مع تماثل الحركتين كحركة الحار والبارد مثل النار والماء إلى العلو وقد يكون واحداً مع تضاد الحركتين كحركة جسم من العلو إلى السفل وبالعكس أو من البياض إلى السواد وبالعكس، أو من غاية نموه إلى ذبوله وبالعكس، أو من انتصابه إلى انتكاسه وبالعكس، ولا لتضاد المحرك لتماثلها مع تضاد المحركتين كما في الحركة الصاعدة للحجر والنار بالقوة القسرية والطبيعية المتضادتين، وتضادها مع اتحاد المحرك كما في حركة الجسم صعوداً وهبوطاً بالإرادة أو بالقسر، ولا لاتضاد الزمان لأنه ليس فيه اختلاف ماهية فضلاً عن التضاد، ولو فرض فتضاد العوارض لا يوجب تضاد المعروضات ولا تضاد ما فيه لأن الصعود والهبوط متضادان اتحاد ما فيه وكذا التسود والتبيض عند اتحاد الطريق فتعين أن يكون تضاد الحركة لتضاد ما منه وما إليه، وتضادهما قد يكون بالذات كما في الحركة من السواد إلى البياض وبالعكس ومن غاية النمو الذي في طبيعة الجسم إلى غاية الذبول وبالعكس، ومن الانتصاب إلى الانتكاس وبالعكس. وما يقال إنه لا تضاد في الحركة الوضعية فمختص بالمستديرة وقد يكون بالعرض كما في الحركة الصاعدة الهابطة بحسب ما بين مبدائهما من التضاد بعارض كون أحدهما في غاية القرب من المركز والبعد من المحيط والآخر بالعكس، وكذا المنتهى.
There is no doubt that the differences in the states of motion are only due to the differences in their objects. So the opposition of motion is not due to the opposition of the moved object because it is a body, and there is no essential opposition in it. And if we consider accidental opposition, then it may be opposed despite the similarity of the two motions, like the motion of the hot and the cold, such as fire and water upward, and it may be one despite the opposition of the two motions, like the motion of a body from upward to downward and vice versa, or from whiteness to blackness and vice versa, or from the extreme of its growth to its decay and vice versa, or from its erectness to its inversion and vice versa. And it is not due to the opposition of the mover, because of their similarity despite the opposition of the two movers, as in the upward motion of a stone and fire by coercive and natural forces which are opposed, and their opposition despite the unity of the mover, as in the motion of a body upward and downward by will or by force. And it is not due to the opposition of time, because there is no difference in its essence, let alone opposition. And if it were supposed, the opposition of accidents does not necessitate the opposition of their substrates. And it is not due to the opposition of what it is in, because ascent and descent are opposed while what they are in is one, similarly blackening and whitening when the path is one. Thus it is determined that the opposition of motion is due to the opposition of its 'from which' and 'to which'. And their opposition may be essential, as in the motion from blackness to whiteness and vice versa, and from the extreme of growth which is in the nature of the body to the extreme of decay and vice versa, and from erectness to inversion and vice versa. And what is said that there is no opposition in positional motion is specific to circular motion. And it may be accidental, as in ascending and descending motion, according to what is between their starting points of opposition due to the accident of one being at the extreme proximity to the center and distance from the periphery, and the other vice versa, and similarly the endpoint.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is an argument establishing that the opposition (tadadd) between two motions is due to the opposition between their starting points and ending points. The author first rejects alternative explanations: It is not due to opposition in the moved object (because it is a body with no inherent opposition), nor due to opposition in the mover (since the same motion can occur with different movers, and opposite motions with the same mover), nor due to opposition in time (time has no specific quiddity), nor due to opposition of accidents necessarily implying opposition of substrates. He then provides evidence by noting that ascent and descent are opposite even though the substrate is one, and similarly blackening and whitening when the path is one. Therefore, the only remaining cause is the opposition of the termini (ma minhu and ma ilayhi). He distinguishes between essential opposition (as in color change) and accidental opposition (as in upward/downward motion relative to center and periphery). This sets the stage for the subsequent discussion.

Key Terms
تضاد
حركة
ما منه
ما إليه
عارض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the opposition of motion might be due to the mover or the moved object.
Correction: The author refutes both: similar motions can have opposite movers, and opposite motions can have the same moved object. The true cause is opposition of termini.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the ultimate cause of opposition between two motions?
A) Opposition of the moved object
B) Opposition of the mover
C) Opposition of time
D) Opposition of the starting and ending points

Key Takeaway
The opposition of two motions is not due to the object, mover, time, or substrate, but solely to the opposition of their starting and ending points.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often think your struggle with a bad habit is because of your nature (moved object) or your circumstances (mover). But this lesson says the real opposition lies in the ends—what you are moving toward. What are the actual ends of your actions today, and are you willing to change them?
?
When you feel conflicted between two choices, do you focus on the difficulty of the path or the superiority of the goal? The author tells you the opposition comes from the termini, not the path. Are you honest about which end you truly desire?
?
You might excuse a wrong action by saying 'that was a different time in my life.' But time has no opposition—time cannot make an action good or bad. Are you hiding behind time instead of confronting the true source of your action?

When Accidental Opposition Implies Subject Opposition
The author answers an objection by qualifying the principle of accidental opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the principle 'opposition of an accident does not imply opposition of its subject' is qualified and applied to the case of motion.

Core Idea
Accidental opposition can imply subject opposition when it makes the definition of opposites true.

In this passage, the author addresses an important objection: if an accident's opposition doesn't imply the subject's opposition, how can the opposition of motion's endpoints cause the motions themselves to be opposite? The answer hinges on a crucial qualification—accidental opposition can indeed imply subject opposition when it is specific enough to satisfy the definition of true opposites. Let's follow the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the objection carefully, then the author's answer. Notice the author does not reject the principle outright but qualifies it.
2
Identify the qualification
The author distinguishes between absolute accidental opposition and specific opposition that makes the definition of two opposites true. Understand this distinction.
The key Arabic terms are 'عارض' (accident) and 'معروض' (subject).
3
Apply to motion
See how the author applies the qualification to ascending and descending motions, showing they fulfill the definition of opposites.
Look for the conditions: two existential realities, cannot coexist in one time from one aspect, utmost difference.
4
Compare with other motions
The author contrasts with non-opposite motions: rectilinear back-and-forth (one species) and curvilinear (no utmost difference). Understand why these do not qualify.
The concept of 'غاية الخلاف' (utmost difference) is crucial.
5
Synthesize the lesson
Summarize the conditional nature of the principle and how it resolves the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : قد ذكروا أن تضاد العارض لا يوجب تضاد المعروض فكيف أوجب تضاد عارض بعض ما يتعلق به الحركة تضاد الحركة مع أن هذا أبعد . . ؟ قلنا مرادهم أن ذلك بمجرده وعلى إطلاقه لا يوجب تضاد المعروض، وأما إذا كان بخصوصه بحيث يوجب صدق حد الضدين على المعروض، أو على ما يتعلق به فلا استبعاد وههنا قد صدق بتضاد الطرفين حد الضدين على الحركتين لأنهما أعني الصاعدة والهابطة أمران وجوديان يمتنع اجتماعهما في زمان واحد من جهة واحدة مع كونهما نوعين من جنس بينهما غاية الخلاف وهذا بخلاف الحركة المستقيمة نقطة المسافة إلى نقطة مع الرجوع عنها إلى الأول لا بطريق الصعود والهبوط فإنهما نوع واحد وبخلاف المستقيمة والمنحنية أو المنحنيتين وإن كانت إحداهما فوق والأخرى تحت فإنهما ليستا على غاية الخلاف لأن بين كل نقطتين قسيا غير متناهية والعظمى أشد انحناء فأشد مخالفة. ولا يجوز أن يعتبر مطلق الانحناء لأنه لا يوجد في الخارج إلا في ضمن معين وكل معين يوجد فما فوقه أشد مخالفة منه وههنا مواضع بحث.
For it is said: They have mentioned that the opposition of an accident does not necessitate the opposition of its subject, so how does the opposition of an accident of something with which motion is connected necessitate the opposition of motion, even though this is more remote? We say: What they mean is that this, by itself and absolutely, does not necessitate the opposition of the subject. But if it is specifically such that it necessitates the truth of the definition of the two opposites (al-diddayn) upon the subject, or upon what is connected to it, then there is no improbability. And here, by the opposition of the two extremes, the definition of the two opposites is truly applied to the two motions, because they, I mean the ascending and descending, are two existential realities that cannot coexist in one time from one aspect, while being two species of a genus between which there is the utmost difference. This is unlike a rectilinear motion from a point of distance to a point with a return to the first not by way of ascent and descent, for they are one species. And unlike rectilinear and curvilinear, or two curvilinear motions, even if one is above and the other below, for they are not at the utmost difference, because between every two points there are infinite arcs, and the larger one is more curved and thus more different. And it is not permissible to consider absolute curvature, because it does not exist externally except within a specific one, and every specific one that exists, what is above it is more different from it. And here are points of investigation.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objector points out a known principle: the opposition of an accident does not entail the opposition of the substance. So how can the opposition of an accidental feature (like the termini of motion) cause the motion itself to be opposite? The author responds by qualifying the principle: it applies only when considered absolutely and by itself. But when the accidental opposition reaches the point that the definition of 'two opposites' applies to the subject or to what is connected to it, then it does cause opposition. In this case, the ascending and descending motions truly fulfill the definition of opposites: they are two existent realities that cannot coexist at the same time in the same respect, and they are two species within a genus that exhibit the utmost difference (ghayat al-khilaf). The author then contrasts this with other cases: a rectilinear motion that goes back and forth along the same line without ascent/descent is not opposite because it is one species; and two curvilinear motions, even if one is above the other, do not reach utmost difference because there are infinitely many degrees of curvature. Thus the objection is refuted by specifying the conditions under which accidental opposition can indeed imply opposition in the subject.

Key Terms
عارض
معروض
ضدين
غاية الخلاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The principle 'opposition of an accident does not imply opposition of its subject' is absolute and unconditional.
Correction: The author shows it is conditional: when accidental opposition is specific and makes the definition of opposites true for the subject, it can imply opposition.

Checkpoint
According to the author, when can the opposition of an accident imply opposition of its subject?
A) Absolutely always
B) Never
C) When it is specific and makes the definition of opposites apply
D) Only in the case of motion

Key Takeaway
The principle that accidental opposition does not imply subject opposition is conditional: it applies only when the accidental opposition is not specific enough to fulfill the definition of true opposites.

Three Investigative Points on Opposition of Motion
The author raises three problematic cases regarding the criteria for opposition in motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three problematic cases that test the criteria for opposition (tadadd) in motion, and how scholars analyzed them.

Core Idea
Opposition in motion requires utmost difference in both starting points and endpoints.

In this passage, the author presents three investigative points that refine our understanding of what makes two motions truly opposite. These cases challenge simplistic definitions and show the depth of kalam analysis. Let's examine each one to see how the criteria apply.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the three enumerated points.
The passage uses technical terms like 'qaws' and 'ghayat al-khilaf'.
2
Understand the first point
The first point discusses an arc tangent to the celestial sphere. Motion along such an arc is at utmost difference and thus opposite to rectilinear motion.
This shows that circular and rectilinear motions can be opposites under the definition.
3
Understand the second point
The second point shows that not all rectilinear ascents and descents are maximally opposite. For example, ascent to fire and descent from it are less opposed than motions toward the sphere or center.
This demonstrates degrees of opposition; true opposition requires utmost difference.
4
Understand the third point
The third point examines the condition that both starting points and endpoints must be opposite. Examples show that if either is the same, the motions are not opposite.
Ibn Sina's example of water motions illustrates this principle.
5
Reflect on the overall lesson
Consider how these points refine the criteria for opposition. Why is it not enough for motions to simply be in opposite directions?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول : إن القوس التي تماس محدب الفلك المحيط في غاية الخلاف فالحركة عليها ينبغي أن تكون ضداً للحركة المستقيمة لصدق الحد بجميع شرائطه. الثاني : إن الصاعدة والهابطة المستقيمتين أيضاً قد لا تكونان على غاية الخلاف كالصعود من وجه الأرض إلى النار والهبوط منها إليه لظهور أن الصعود إلى الفلك أشد مخالفة لذلك الهبوط، والهبوط إلى مركز الأرض أشد مخالفة لذلك الصعود . الثالث : إن ظاهر كلامهم هو أن المعتبر في تضاد الحركتين تضاد مبدأيهما وتضاد منتهيهما جميعاً ، فالصعود والهبوط من المركز والمحيط إلى حيز من الهواء مثلا لا يكونان متضادين لاتحاد المنتهى، وكذا الصعود والهبوط منه إلى المحيط والمركز لاتحاد المبدأ، وقد صرح ابن سينا بأنه لا تضاد بين حركتي الماء بالطبع من فوق الهواء ومن تحت الأرض لأنهما ينتهيان إلى نهاية واحدة، ولا يظهر لهذا سبب سوى ما ذكره الإمام : وهو أنهما ليستا على غاية التباعد لأن البعد بين حركة النار وحركة الأرض أكثر من البعد بين الماء من المركز وهبوطه عن المحيط (وعلى هذا لا يتحقق التضاد في صعود الماء من تحت الأرض وهبوطه من فوق الهواء. (1) القوس : يذكر ويؤنث والجمع قسي، وأقواس .
The first: The arc which touches the convexity of the encompassing sphere is at the utmost difference, so motion upon it should be opposite to rectilinear motion, because the definition is truly applied with all its conditions. The second: The rectilinear ascending and descending motions also may not be at the utmost difference, like the ascent from the face of the earth to the fire and the descent from it to it, because it is evident that the ascent to the sphere is more contrary to that descent, and the descent to the center of the earth is more contrary to that ascent. The third: The apparent meaning of their words is that what is considered in the opposition of two motions is the opposition of their starting points and the opposition of their endpoints both together. So ascent and descent from the center and the periphery to a region of air, for example, are not opposite due to the unity of the endpoint, and similarly ascent and descent from it to the periphery and center due to the unity of the starting point. Ibn Sina has stated that there is no opposition between the natural motions of water from above the air and from under the earth, because they end at one endpoint. No reason appears for this except what the Imam mentioned: that they are not at the utmost distance, because the distance between the motion of fire and the motion of earth is greater than the distance between water from the center and its descent from the periphery. And accordingly, opposition is not realized in the ascent of water from under the earth and its descent from above the air. (1) al-qaws: it is masculine and feminine, plural qisiyy and aqwas.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage lists three investigative points (mawadi' bahth) that test the criterion for opposition (tadadd) in motion. The first point considers the arc (qaws) tangent to the convexity of the encompassing sphere; such an arc is at the utmost difference, so motion along it should be opposite to rectilinear motion, satisfying the definition of opposites. The second point notes that even rectilinear ascent and descent may not always be at the utmost difference; for example, ascent from the earth's surface to the sphere of fire and descent from it back to earth are not maximally opposed because there are more opposed motions (ascent to the celestial sphere is more contrary to that descent, and descent to the center is more contrary to that ascent). The third point examines the view that both the starting points and endpoints must be opposite for two motions to be opposite. It gives examples where either the endpoint is the same (ascent and descent from center and periphery to a neutral zone) or the starting point is the same, resulting in no opposition. It cites Ibn Sina's statement about water's natural motions, which end at the same point, and explains that the reason is the lack of utmost distance. The footnote clarifies the word 'qaws'.

Key Terms
قوس
غاية الخلاف
مبدأ
منتهى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any ascending and descending motions are automatically opposite.
Correction: True opposition requires utmost difference in both starting points and endpoints, as shown by the examples.

Checkpoint
According to the third investigative point, what is required for two motions to be considered opposite?
A) Only the starting points must be opposite
B) Only the endpoints must be opposite
C) Both starting points and endpoints must be opposite
D) The motions must be rectilinear

Key Takeaway
Two motions are truly opposite only when both their starting points and endpoints are at utmost difference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that two things are truly opposite only when both their starting points and endpoints are at utmost difference. Where in your life have you settled for being 'different' from falsehood without ensuring your endpoint is the highest truth? What will you change to make your spiritual journey genuinely opposite to misguidance?
?
The author critiques motions that share an endpoint, showing they are not truly opposed. Do you sometimes pursue actions that start with good intentions but end at the same worldly goal as everyone else? How can you ensure your actions end at the utmost goal that separates you from the crowd?
?
Ibn Sina's example of water motions reveals that apparent opposites may not be truly opposite. Are there beliefs or habits you consider 'opposite' to sin but that, on examination, share the same endpoint as sin? Commit to one concrete step to align both your starting point and endpoint with Allah's pleasure.

The Opposition of Place-Based Motions
The author asserts and explains the opposition of place-based motions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the opposition of motions in place is confined to ascending and descending relative to the center and circumference, and how this relates to the concept of necessary accident.

Core Idea
True opposition of motions arises from opposed directions, not mere spatial separation.

In this passage, the author clarifies a key principle: not all motions can be considered opposites. Only those with directly opposed directions—up and down—qualify. This distinction rests on the notion of a necessary accident that defines the extremes of proximity and distance.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's claim about opposition
Start by reading the Arabic passage where the author states that opposition in place-based motions is only between ascending and descending. Notice the reference to the center and circumference.
The author uses 'utmost distance' as a criterion.
2
Understand the answer about direction
The author then explains that opposition is not due to the physical points but due to the direction (جهة). The directions of up and down are naturally distinct and different in type.
This is a key shift from spatial to directional opposition.
3
Consider the concept of necessary accident
The author introduces 'necessary accident' (عارض لازم) as the basis for opposition: extreme proximity to the circumference and distance from the center. This is what makes up and down opposites.
Other directions do not have this necessary accident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التضاد
الحركات الأينية إلا بين الصعود من المركز إلى المحيط، والهبوط من المحيط) (۱) إلى المركز إذ فيما سوى ذلك لا يتحقق ما اعبروه ههنا في من غاية التباعد، وكون ضد الواحد واحداً، وهم مصرحون بأن حركتي الحجر علواً وسفلاً بالقسر والطبع متضادتان .
والجواب : أن تضاد الحركة لتضاد ما منه وما إليه ليس من حيث الحصول فيهما، إذ لا حركة حينئذ بل من حيث التوجه فيعتبر حال الجهة وجها العلو والسفل متميزان بالطبع مختلفان بالنوع، متضادتان بعارض لازم وهو غاية القرب من المحيط والبعد عنه بخلاف سائر الجهات .
الرابع : : أن الإمام قد اعتبر في تضاد الحركة تضاد المبدأ والمنتهى من حيث وصف المبدئية والمنتهية، وذكر أن التعلق الذاتي للحركة لما كان بنفس الوصفين دون ،الذاتين، إذ لو لم يعرض للنقطتين كونها مبدأ وغاية للحركة لم يكن للحركة تعلق بهما أوجب تضاد الإطلاق (۲) تضاد الحركات .
فإن قيل : موجب تضاد الحركتين تضاد مبدأيهما، وتضاد منتهيهما لاتضاد المبدأ والمنتهى قلنا معنى الكلام لأن المبدأ والمنتهى لما كانا متضادين كانت الصاعدة والهابطة مبدأهما متضدين لكونهما مبدأ ومنتهى للصاعدة، وكذلك منتهاهما لكونهما مبدأ ومنهى للهابطة فإن قيل : فيلزم التضاد بين كل حركة مستقيمة من نقطة إلى أخرى مع الرجوع عنها إلى الأولى بل المستديرة أيضاً كما إذا تحرك جسم من أول الحمل إلى أول الميزان، ثم رجع عنه إلى أول الحمل بحيث يكون ممر الحركتين على الحمل، والثور والجوزاء والسرطان والأسد والسنبلة ويتحقق البداية والنهاية بالفعل، فلا يندفع بما قيل إن الحركة على التوالي لا تضاد الحركة على خلاف التوالي لأن كلاً منهما تفعل مثل ما تفعل الأخرى لكن في النصفين على التبادل مثلاً المنحدر من السرطان إلى الجدي على التوالي يكون مسافته (۳) الأسد والسنبلة والميزان والعقرب ،والقوس والمنحدر من السرطان إلى الجدي على خلاف التوالي يكون مسافته (۱) الجوزاء والثور والحمل والحوت والدلو، والصعود بالعكس، فقد فعل كل منهما ما فعله الآخر لكن في النصف الآخر. قلنا: لو ثبت الخلاف بالماهية وغاية الخلاف إلتزام التضاد وهم إنما نفوا التضاد عن الحركات المستديرة الوضعية كحركة الرحا، وما ذكرت من الحركتين بين الحمل والميزان حركة أينية على الاستدارة كحركة النمل على الرحى .
The opposition of motions in place is only between ascending from the center to the circumference and descending from the circumference to the center, because in other than that, what they considered here of utmost distance is not realized, and that the opposite of one is one, and they explicitly state that the two motions of a stone upward and downward, by coercion and by nature, are opposites. The answer: that the opposition of motion is due to the opposition of its 'from which' and 'to which', not in terms of occurrence in them, since there is no motion then, but in terms of direction. Thus, the state of direction is considered: the directions of up and down are naturally distinct, different in type, and are opposites due to a necessary accident, which is the utmost proximity to the circumference and distance from it, unlike other directions. Fourth: The Imam considered in the opposition of motion the opposition of the starting point and the endpoint in terms of the description of being a starting point and being an endpoint. He mentioned that the essential attachment of motion is to the two descriptions themselves, not to the two substances, because if the two points were not considered as a starting point and an endpoint for the motion, the motion would not have an attachment to them that necessitates the opposition of the motions. If it is said: The cause of the opposition of two motions is the opposition of their starting points and the opposition of their endpoints with the opposition of the starting point and endpoint? We say: The meaning of the statement is that since the starting point and endpoint are opposites, the ascending and descending motions are opposites because they are starting point and endpoint for the ascending motion, and similarly their endpoints are starting point and endpoint for the descending motion. If it is said: Then opposition would be necessary between every rectilinear motion from a point to another and the return from it to the first, even for circular motion. For example, if a body moves from the beginning of Aries to the beginning of Libra, then returns from it to the beginning of Aries such that the path of the two motions passes through Aries, Taurus, Gemini, Cancer, Leo, and Virgo, and the beginning and end are actualized. Then it cannot be refuted by what is said that motion in order is not opposite to motion in reverse order, because each of them does what the other does, but in opposite halves. For example, the descending from Cancer to Capricorn in order has its distance (3) Leo, Virgo, Libra, Scorpio, Sagittarius; and the descending from Cancer to Capricorn in reverse order has its distance (1) Gemini, Taurus, Aries, Pisces, Aquarius; and the ascending is the opposite. Thus, each of them has done what the other did, but in the other half. We say: If the difference in essence is established, and the ultimate difference entails opposition, but they only denied opposition for positional circular motions like the motion of a millstone, and what you mentioned of the two motions between Aries and Libra is a motion in place on a circular path like the motion of an ant on a millstone.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument about the nature of opposition (تضاد) in motions. The author first asserts that opposition in place-based motions (الحركات الأينية) only occurs between ascending (صعود) and descending (هبوط) relative to the center and circumference, because only there is the greatest distance realized, and the opposite of one is one. He then provides an answer to an implicit objection: the opposition of motions is not due to the actual spatial points of occurrence (الحصول فيهما) but due to the direction (التوجه). The directions of up and down are naturally distinct and different in type, and they are opposites by a necessary accident (عارض لازم), namely extreme proximity to the circumference and distance from it. Next, the author mentions the view of the Imam (likely al-Razi) who considers opposition of motions based on the opposition of the starting point (مبدأ) and endpoint (منتهى) as descriptions (وصف المبدئية والمنتهية), not as substances (الذاتين). He explains that the essential attachment of motion is to these descriptions, so if the points were not considered as starting point and endpoint, no opposition would arise. Then an objection is raised: if the cause of opposition is the opposition of starting points and endpoints, then every rectilinear motion and its return would be opposite, even circular motions. The objector gives an example of a body moving from the beginning of Aries to Libra and back. The author answers that this example is actually a circular motion (حركة أينية على الاستدارة) like an ant on a millstone, and circular motions are not subject to opposition in the same way. Thus, the objection fails.

Key Terms
تضاد
حركة
جهة
عارض لازم
صعود
هبوط
مركز
محيط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any two motions in opposite spatial directions (e.g., north vs. south) are considered opposites in the same way as up and down.
Correction: Opposition of motions requires a necessary accident of extreme proximity and distance, which only applies to up and down relative to the center and circumference.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what makes the upward and downward motions opposites?
A) They occur in opposite directions spatially.
B) They have opposite starting and ending points.
C) They are associated with a necessary accident of extreme proximity to the circumference and distance from it.
D) They are both natural motions.

Key Takeaway
Only motions with opposite directions (up/down) are truly opposed because of the necessary accident of extreme proximity to the circumference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your life, what two directions (e.g., toward God and away from Him) are truly opposites, not just different? How does the lesson's insistence on 'utmost distance' (ghayat al-taba'ud) challenge you to consider whether you are making any real progress toward the center or merely shifting between intermediate positions?
?
The source says that opposition of motion is due to the 'from which' and 'to which'—not the endpoints themselves, but the direction toward them. What is the 'direction' of your heart right now? Are you ascending toward the circumference (distraction, pride) or descending toward the center (humility, submission)? Be honest: which motion defines you today?
?
If only up and down are truly opposite because of a 'necessary accident', what necessary accident (inseparable circumstance) in your life determines whether your actions are moving you toward truth or away from it? Can you identify one such circumstance that you have been ignoring?

The Imam's View and the Circular Motion Objection
The author presents the Imam's view on opposition of motions and refutes an objection concerning circular motions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the opposition of motions is traced to the opposition of starting points and endpoints as descriptions, and why circular motions are not considered opposites.

Core Idea
Opposition of motions depends on the descriptions 'starting point' and 'endpoint', not on the spatial points themselves.

The author now discusses a more technical view attributed to the Imam (Fakhr al-Din al-Razi), who argues that the essential attachment of motion is to the descriptions of beginning and end, not to the actual points. An objection raises the problem of rectilinear and circular motions, and the author refutes it by distinguishing circular motions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Imam's view on opposition
Read the passage where the Imam states that opposition of motion is based on the opposition of starting point and endpoint as descriptions (وصف المبدئية والمنتهية), not the substances themselves.
This is a shift from considering actual points to considering their roles.
2
Understand the objection about rectilinear and circular motions
The objector argues that if opposition is based on starting/ending points, then every rectilinear motion and its return would be opposite, even circular motions. An example is given using zodiac signs.
The objection attempts to show that this view leads to absurd consequences.
3
See the author's answer distinguishing circular motions
The author responds that circular motions are not subject to opposition in the same way; the example given is actually a circular motion, not a rectilinear one, and thus the objection fails.
The answer hinges on the nature of circular vs. rectilinear paths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التضاد
الحركات الأينية إلا بين الصعود من المركز إلى المحيط، والهبوط من المحيط) (۱) إلى المركز إذ فيما سوى ذلك لا يتحقق ما اعبروه ههنا في من غاية التباعد، وكون ضد الواحد واحداً، وهم مصرحون بأن حركتي الحجر علواً وسفلاً بالقسر والطبع متضادتان .
والجواب : أن تضاد الحركة لتضاد ما منه وما إليه ليس من حيث الحصول فيهما، إذ لا حركة حينئذ بل من حيث التوجه فيعتبر حال الجهة وجها العلو والسفل متميزان بالطبع مختلفان بالنوع، متضادتان بعارض لازم وهو غاية القرب من المحيط والبعد عنه بخلاف سائر الجهات .
الرابع : : أن الإمام قد اعتبر في تضاد الحركة تضاد المبدأ والمنتهى من حيث وصف المبدئية والمنتهية، وذكر أن التعلق الذاتي للحركة لما كان بنفس الوصفين دون ،الذاتين، إذ لو لم يعرض للنقطتين كونها مبدأ وغاية للحركة لم يكن للحركة تعلق بهما أوجب تضاد الإطلاق (۲) تضاد الحركات .
فإن قيل : موجب تضاد الحركتين تضاد مبدأيهما، وتضاد منتهيهما لاتضاد المبدأ والمنتهى قلنا معنى الكلام لأن المبدأ والمنتهى لما كانا متضادين كانت الصاعدة والهابطة مبدأهما متضدين لكونهما مبدأ ومنتهى للصاعدة، وكذلك منتهاهما لكونهما مبدأ ومنهى للهابطة فإن قيل : فيلزم التضاد بين كل حركة مستقيمة من نقطة إلى أخرى مع الرجوع عنها إلى الأولى بل المستديرة أيضاً كما إذا تحرك جسم من أول الحمل إلى أول الميزان، ثم رجع عنه إلى أول الحمل بحيث يكون ممر الحركتين على الحمل، والثور والجوزاء والسرطان والأسد والسنبلة ويتحقق البداية والنهاية بالفعل، فلا يندفع بما قيل إن الحركة على التوالي لا تضاد الحركة على خلاف التوالي لأن كلاً منهما تفعل مثل ما تفعل الأخرى لكن في النصفين على التبادل مثلاً المنحدر من السرطان إلى الجدي على التوالي يكون مسافته (۳) الأسد والسنبلة والميزان والعقرب ،والقوس والمنحدر من السرطان إلى الجدي على خلاف التوالي يكون مسافته (۱) الجوزاء والثور والحمل والحوت والدلو، والصعود بالعكس، فقد فعل كل منهما ما فعله الآخر لكن في النصف الآخر. قلنا: لو ثبت الخلاف بالماهية وغاية الخلاف إلتزام التضاد وهم إنما نفوا التضاد عن الحركات المستديرة الوضعية كحركة الرحا، وما ذكرت من الحركتين بين الحمل والميزان حركة أينية على الاستدارة كحركة النمل على الرحى .
The opposition of motions in place is only between ascending from the center to the circumference and descending from the circumference to the center, because in other than that, what they considered here of utmost distance is not realized, and that the opposite of one is one, and they explicitly state that the two motions of a stone upward and downward, by coercion and by nature, are opposites. The answer: that the opposition of motion is due to the opposition of its 'from which' and 'to which', not in terms of occurrence in them, since there is no motion then, but in terms of direction. Thus, the state of direction is considered: the directions of up and down are naturally distinct, different in type, and are opposites due to a necessary accident, which is the utmost proximity to the circumference and distance from it, unlike other directions. Fourth: The Imam considered in the opposition of motion the opposition of the starting point and the endpoint in terms of the description of being a starting point and being an endpoint. He mentioned that the essential attachment of motion is to the two descriptions themselves, not to the two substances, because if the two points were not considered as a starting point and an endpoint for the motion, the motion would not have an attachment to them that necessitates the opposition of the motions. If it is said: The cause of the opposition of two motions is the opposition of their starting points and the opposition of their endpoints with the opposition of the starting point and endpoint? We say: The meaning of the statement is that since the starting point and endpoint are opposites, the ascending and descending motions are opposites because they are starting point and endpoint for the ascending motion, and similarly their endpoints are starting point and endpoint for the descending motion. If it is said: Then opposition would be necessary between every rectilinear motion from a point to another and the return from it to the first, even for circular motion. For example, if a body moves from the beginning of Aries to the beginning of Libra, then returns from it to the beginning of Aries such that the path of the two motions passes through Aries, Taurus, Gemini, Cancer, Leo, and Virgo, and the beginning and end are actualized. Then it cannot be refuted by what is said that motion in order is not opposite to motion in reverse order, because each of them does what the other does, but in opposite halves. For example, the descending from Cancer to Capricorn in order has its distance (3) Leo, Virgo, Libra, Scorpio, Sagittarius; and the descending from Cancer to Capricorn in reverse order has its distance (1) Gemini, Taurus, Aries, Pisces, Aquarius; and the ascending is the opposite. Thus, each of them has done what the other did, but in the other half. We say: If the difference in essence is established, and the ultimate difference entails opposition, but they only denied opposition for positional circular motions like the motion of a millstone, and what you mentioned of the two motions between Aries and Libra is a motion in place on a circular path like the motion of an ant on a millstone.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument about the nature of opposition (تضاد) in motions. The author first asserts that opposition in place-based motions (الحركات الأينية) only occurs between ascending (صعود) and descending (هبوط) relative to the center and circumference, because only there is the greatest distance realized, and the opposite of one is one. He then provides an answer to an implicit objection: the opposition of motions is not due to the actual spatial points of occurrence (الحصول فيهما) but due to the direction (التوجه). The directions of up and down are naturally distinct and different in type, and they are opposites by a necessary accident (عارض لازم), namely extreme proximity to the circumference and distance from it. Next, the author mentions the view of the Imam (likely al-Razi) who considers opposition of motions based on the opposition of the starting point (مبدأ) and endpoint (منتهى) as descriptions (وصف المبدئية والمنتهية), not as substances (الذاتين). He explains that the essential attachment of motion is to these descriptions, so if the points were not considered as starting point and endpoint, no opposition would arise. Then an objection is raised: if the cause of opposition is the opposition of starting points and endpoints, then every rectilinear motion and its return would be opposite, even circular motions. The objector gives an example of a body moving from the beginning of Aries to Libra and back. The author answers that this example is actually a circular motion (حركة أينية على الاستدارة) like an ant on a millstone, and circular motions are not subject to opposition in the same way. Thus, the objection fails.

Key Terms
مبدأ
منتهى
وصف المبدئية
الذاتين
تعلق ذاتي
تضاد الإطلاق
حركة مستقيمة
حركة مستديرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any two motions that are reciprocal (back-and-forth along the same line) are necessarily opposites.
Correction: Opposition requires that the motions have opposite descriptions of beginning and end; circular motions, even if they traverse the same arc, are not considered opposites because they lack a true starting/ending point distinction.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the objection about circular motions?
A) Because circular motions are not real motions.
B) Because the example given is not actually a motion.
C) Because the motions in the example are circular, not rectilinear, and circular motions are not subject to opposition.
D) Because the objector misunderstood the definition of 'starting point'.

Key Takeaway
Opposition of motions relies on opposition of descriptions of beginning and end; circular motions do not qualify.
