The Fourfold Division of Motion
Sanusi enumerates the four types of division of motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how motion is divided into four types according to time, distance, quality, and the parts of the moving object, and the condition for actual division in place-based motion.

Core Idea
Motion divides by time, distance, quality, and the moving body's parts.

The author begins by explaining the fourfold division of motion. He shows that motion can be divided based on the division of time, distance, quantity of growth, quality, and even the parts of the moving object. However, in place-based motion, this division becomes actual only when a part becomes separated from the whole. This sets the stage for understanding the relationship between motion and its subject.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the division into four
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses a compressed style.
2
Identify each type of division
The passage describes divisions by time, distance, quantity, quality, and parts of the moving object. Find each one and notice how the author defines it.
3
Understand the condition for place-based motion
In place-based motion, the division into parts becomes actual only when a part separates from the whole, because interior parts do not leave their places.
This distinction is important for later discussions.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why the author starts with this division. It establishes the framework for the correlation between motion, time, and change.
Connect this to the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : وأما انقسامها أربعة :
فإنقسام الزمان وهو ظاهر وما فيه فإن الحركة إلى نصف المسافة أو نصف الكمية الحاصلة بالنمو أو إحدى (۲) الكيفيتين المتوسطتين في تسود الأبيض نصف الحركة إلى الكل، وما له لأن ما يقوم من الحركة لكل جزء من المتحرك غير ما يقوم بالآخر، وهذا في الأينية إنما يصير بالفعل إذا عرض للجزء انفصال لأن الأجزاء (۳) ) لا سيما الباطنة لا تفارق أيونها ) .
لاخفاء
في تطابق الحركة والزمان وما يقع فيه التغير من المقادير والكيفيات والأيون والأوضاع فعند انقسام أحد الأمور الثلاثة، ينقسم الآخران ضرورة وأمر المبدأ والمنتهى ظاهر وفي المحرك تفصيل، وهو أنه قد لا ينقسم، وقد لا ينقسم وبتقدير الانقسام قد يقوى البعض منه على التحريك وقد لا يقوى وبتقدير القوة هل يكون بعض الأثر أثر البعض. وبالجملة فالكلام فيه طويل، وأما المتحرك فمن حيث أنه محل للحركة وانقسام المحل موجب لانقسام الحال كما(٤) ينبغي أن يكون انقسامها بانقسامه ظاهر لكنه خفي من جهة الخفاء في أن القابل للانقسام من الحركة هل هو حال في المتحرك حلول السريان كالبياض في الجسم، وقد اختص ذلك في الحركة بمزيد
He said: As for its division into four: the division of time is apparent, and what is in it: motion to half the distance or half the quantity obtained by growth or one of the two intermediate qualities in blackening white is half the motion to the whole; and what belongs to it because what arises from motion for each part of the moving object is other than what arises for the other. And this in place-based motion becomes actual only if separation occurs for the part, because the parts, especially the internal ones, do not leave their places. No doubt about the correspondence of motion and time and what change occurs in quantities, qualities, places, and positions. So when one of the three things divides, the other two divide necessarily. The matter of the starting point and endpoint is apparent. And regarding the mover, there is detail: it may not divide, and it may not divide; and assuming division, some of it may be strong enough to cause motion and some may not; and assuming strength, is some effect the effect of some [part]? In short, the discussion is lengthy. As for the moved object, inasmuch as it is a locus for motion, and the division of the locus necessitates the division of the accident, as it should be, its division by its division is apparent, but it is hidden due to the obscurity in whether the divisible part of motion is inherent in the moved object by a permeating inherence like whiteness in a body, and that is specific to motion with an increase.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration and explanation of the fourfold division of motion and its correlation with time, the moving object, and the mover. The author states that motion is divided according to the division of time, which is apparent. Motion itself is divided by distance, quantity of growth, quality (e.g., intermediate qualities in blackening), and by the parts of the moving object (ما له). In place-based motion, division becomes actual only when a part becomes separated. The correspondence (تطابق) between motion, time, and what undergoes change—quantities, qualities, places, positions—is emphasized: if one of these three divides, the other two divide necessarily. The discussion then turns to the mover (المحرك), which may or may not be divisible; if divisible, some parts may have the power to move and some may not. The moved object (المتحرك), as a locus for motion, entails that division of the locus forces division of the accident. However, it is obscure whether the divisible part of motion inheres in the moved object by permeation (حلول السريان) like whiteness in a body, and this was specifically discussed for motion with increase (مزيد).

Key Terms
انقسام
زمان
كمية
كيفية
أينية
انفصال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Motion is only divisible by time.
Correction: The author shows it is also divisible by distance, quality, and the parts of the moving object.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition does the division of motion into parts become actual in place-based motion?
A) When the motion is divided by time.
B) When a part separates from the whole.
C) When the quality changes.
D) When the distance is halved.

Key Takeaway
Motion is divided into four types, and in place-based motion, actual division of motion into parts requires separation of a part.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that every motion is divisible by time, distance, quality, and body parts. If even the smallest movement is analyzable, how does that press you to consider the accountability of every conscious and unconscious motion you make? Will you hold yourself to a higher standard of awareness in your movements from now on?
?
In place-based motion, internal parts do not leave their places unless separated. Think about your heart and your tongue when you pray: do your inner limbs (your sincerity, your focus) actually move toward Allah, or do they remain stationary while your body prays? What will you do today to make your internal parts truly move with your worship?

The Necessary Correspondence of Motion, Time, and Change
Sanusi states the necessary correspondence between motion, time, and change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the necessary correspondence between motion, time, and the changing subject, and how the division of one entails the division of the others.

Core Idea
Motion, time, and change necessarily correspond in division.

The author moves from the division of motion to the necessary relationship between motion, time, and the subject of change. He asserts that there is a correspondence such that when one of the three divides, the other two divide as well. This principle is foundational for understanding the interdependence of motion with time and the changing entity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three things
The passage mentions motion, time, and what change occurs in (quantities, qualities, places, positions). Find these three.
2
Understand the principle of correspondence
The author says when one of these three divides, the other two divide necessarily. This is the key point.
This is a necessary relationship, not accidental.
3
Note the beginning and end
The author says the matter of the starting point and endpoint is apparent. Reflect on why this is obvious.
This may refer to the limits of motion, time, and change.
4
Reflect on the implication
How does this correspondence affect our understanding of motion? Consider that motion cannot be considered independently of time and the changing object.
This connects to the next lesson on the mover and moved object.

The Mover and the Moved Object: Divisibility and Inherence
Sanusi discusses the divisibility of the mover and the inherence of motion in the moved object.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the discussion on the divisibility of the mover and the moved object, and the subtlety of motion's inherence in the moved object, especially in motion of increase.

Core Idea
The mover may or may not be divisible; the moved object forces division of motion, yet inherence is subtle.

The author concludes the passage with a detailed discussion of the mover and the moved object. Regarding the mover, he raises questions about its divisibility and the varying strength of its parts. Regarding the moved object, he explains that as the locus of motion, its division necessitates the division of the accident of motion, but the exact nature of motion's inherence is complex, especially in the case of increase.

Guided Path
1
Read the section on the mover
The passage presents possibilities: the mover may not divide; if it does, parts may have varying power; if powerful, whether each part produces its own effect is unclear.
The author admits this discussion is lengthy.
2
Read the section on the moved object
The principle is that division of the locus (moved object) forces division of the accident (motion). However, the mode of inherence is obscure.
3
Understand the subtlety
The author asks whether the divisible part of motion inheres by permeation (like whiteness) or not, and notes this is specific to motion with increase.
This distinguishes types of motion.
4
Reflect on the overall lesson
Consider how this discussion fits with the previous lessons on division and correspondence.
The mover and moved object are key components in the analysis of motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

The Quantitative Division of Motion: Distance and Time
The author explains the condition for quantitative division of motion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the quantitative division of motion depends on the division of distance or time, not on the division of the moving object itself.

Core Idea
Quantitative division of motion requires dividing distance or time.

This passage distinguishes between dividing motion by dividing the moving object and the quantitative division into fractions like half or third. The author clarifies that true quantitative division of motion is only possible if the distance or time is divided. This distinction is crucial for understanding the nature of motion in Islamic philosophical theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's rhythm come through.
2
Identify the two types of division
The passage mentions a division that results from separation of parts of the moving object, and a quantitative division that yields halves, thirds, etc. Notice how they are different.
3
Find the condition for quantitative division
Look for the phrase 'فلا يتصور إلا بانقسام المسافة أو الزمان'. This states the necessary condition.
The author says quantitative division is inconceivable without dividing distance or time.
4
Reflect on why distance or time must be divided
Think about motion as continuous change. How could you split it into half or quarter without splitting the path or duration?
This connects to the idea that motion's extension is measured by space or time.
5
Connect to broader context
Consider how this fits into the larger discussion of motion in kalam. Quantitative division is a tool for analyzing motion mathematically.
This lesson provides a foundational distinction.

شبیه خفاء، فإن أجزاء المتحرك لا تفارق أمكنتها بالكلية، بل تشبه أن تكون الأجزاء الباطنة لا تفارق أمكنتها أصلاً نعم لو عرض للأجزاء انفصال كان للحركة انقسام بالانقسام في العرض لكن التغير التدريجي المسمى بالحركة على حاله وعلى امتداده، فإن سمي مثل هذا انقساماً للحركة بانقسام المتحرك فلا مشاحة، وأما الانقسام الكمي الذي هو تكثير امتدادها الوهمي إلى ماله من الفرضية بحيث يحصل اسم النصف والثلث والربع ونحو ذلك فلا يتصور إلا بانقسام المسافة أو الزمان .
A resemblance of concealment: for the parts of the moving thing do not completely leave their places; rather the inner parts seem not to leave their places at all. Yes, if separation occurs to the parts, then motion has a division according to division in the accident (عرض). But the gradual change called motion remains as it is and upon its extension. So if such is called a division of motion by the division of the moving thing, there is no objection. As for the quantitative division, which is the multiplication of its imaginary extension into what it has from the hypothetical (الفرضية) such that the name of half, third, quarter and the like is obtained, it is not conceivable except through the division of distance or time.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage clarifies the condition for quantitative division of motion. The author begins by noting that parts of a moving object do not completely leave their places; particularly, inner parts may not leave at all. However, if the parts become separated, then motion can be divided according to the division of the object in terms of accident. Despite that, the gradual change that is motion remains continuous. If someone calls this a division of motion by division of the object, there is no disagreement. Then he distinguishes quantitative division: it is the multiplication of the imaginary extension of motion into parts like half, third, etc. Such division is only conceivable if the distance or the time is divided. In other words, quantitative division of motion depends on division of spatial extension or temporal duration. This is a technical distinction in the analysis of motion.

الانقسام الكمي
المسافة
الزمان
الفرضية

According to the text, what is required for quantitative division of motion?
A) Division of the moving object
B) Division of distance or time
C) Division of accident
D) Division of intensity

Key Takeaway
Quantitative division of motion is only conceivable through division of distance or time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own spiritual journey (sulūk), do you measure progress by dividing time into days and years, or by milestones achieved? Does this lesson's distinction between 'quantitative division through time or distance' challenge you to think about how you evaluate your own growth?
?
When you plan acts of worship (e.g., reciting a portion of Qur'an, giving a fraction of wealth), do you assume that the quantity itself has value, or do you consider the continuity and intention behind it? How does this lesson's teaching that motion's quantitative division depends on something external (distance/time) speak to the danger of reducing worship to mere numbers?
?
If motion's quantitative division is only a mental construct (based on distance/time), then the 'half' or 'third' of your daily effort has no reality apart from your measuring. Are you measuring your life by Allah's scale or by your own invented fractions? What would it mean for you to abandon the urge to quantify and instead focus on the continuous quality of your submission?

The Opposition of Rest and Its Types
Classification of rest and its opposition, with a refutation of composition in rest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how rest is classified into natural, forced, and voluntary types, and why rest cannot be composite, distinguishing it from motion.

Core Idea
Rest does not compose; it simply is—or is not—depending on nature, force, or will.

In this passage, the author examines rest (sukūn) and how it is opposed due to its location or quality. He categorizes rest into natural, forced, and voluntary, and clarifies a common confusion: rest is never composite, unlike motion. This distinction is crucial for understanding the behavior of bodies.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the definitions and examples provided.
2
Identify the three types of rest
List the three types: natural, forced, voluntary. Note the example for each: stone on ground, stone suspended, bird standing.
Observe that natural rest needs no external cause.
3
Understand the objection and answer
The author refutes the idea that human rest is composite of natural and voluntary. See that the will only removes the intention to move, so rest remains natural.
This is a key nuance.
4
Contrast rest with motion
Note that motion can have composition and intensification (like a stone thrown downward), but rest cannot. This distinction is foundational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : وتضاد السكون) يكون لتضاد ما فيه كالسكون في المكان الأعلى والأسفل، أو في الحرارة أو البرودة، ويكون طبيعياً وقسرياً وإرادياً ومستنداً لطبيعي، هو الطبيعة على الإطلاق، ولا يتصور في السكون المركب وسكون الإنسان(۱) الإقسام في المكان الطبيعي، وأثر الإرادة ترك إزالته) . لتضاد ما فيه إذ لا عبرة فيه بتضاد الساكن والمسكن والزمان على ما مر ، ولا تعلق للسكون بما منه وما إليه ،قوله ويكون أي السكون طبيعياً كسكون الحجر على الأرض، وقسرياً كسكونه معلقاً في الهواء ، أو إرادياً كوقوف الطير في الهواء، والطبيعي لا يفتقر إلى مقارنة أمر غير طبيعي كما في الحركة بل يستند إلى الطبيعة مطلقاً، لأن الجسم إذا خلى وطبعه لم يكن له بد من موضع معين لا تطلب مفارقته ولا يتصور في السكون تركب، وإنما تعرض البساطة والتركب للحركة مر في البحث اليابق . كما فإن قيل : سكون الإنسان على الأرض مركب من الطبيعي والإرادي قلنا : لا بل هو واحد وإنما يتوهم التعدد في علته، والتحقيق أنها الطبيعية فقط، وأثر الإرادة ترك إزالته إلى الحركة. فإن كلا من الطبيعة والإرادة والقاسر، إنما يصير تمام علة السكون عند عدم رجحان علة الحركة، وهذا بخلاف الحركة، فإنها لما كانت تقبل الشدة والضعف جاز اجتماع علتين على حركة واحدة كما في الحجر المرمى إلى تحت فظاهر أنها ليست من التركيب شيء وإنما هو اشتداد .
He said: And the opposition of rest is due to the opposition of that in which it is, like rest in the highest and lowest place, or in heat or cold. And it is natural, forced, and voluntary, and is based on the natural, which is nature absolutely. And composition is not conceivable in rest, and the rest of a human being in the natural place; the effect of will is leaving its removal. Due to the opposition of that in which it is, for no consideration is given to the opposition of the resting thing, the place, or the time, as has passed. And rest has no relation to its 'from' and 'to'. His statement: 'And it is' — i.e., rest is natural like the rest of a stone on the ground, forced like its rest when suspended in the air, or voluntary like the standing of a bird in the air. The natural does not require the accompaniment of something unnatural as in motion, but rather is based on nature absolutely, because if a body is left to its nature, it necessarily has a specific place which it does not seek to leave. Composition is not conceivable in rest; rather simplicity and composition occur in motion, as has passed in the previous discussion. So if it is said: The rest of a human being on the ground is composite of natural and voluntary, we say: No, rather it is one, and multiplicity is only imagined in its cause, and the reality is that it is only natural, and the effect of will is leaving its removal to motion. For each of nature, will, and force only becomes the complete cause of rest when the cause of motion is not predominant. This is unlike motion, for since it admits intensity and weakness, it is possible for two causes to combine in one motion, as in a stone thrown downward; it is apparent that there is no composition in it, but rather intensification.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage discusses the opposition (تضاد) of rest (سكون) and its types. The author first explains that rest is opposed due to the opposition of that in which it is (تضاد ما فيه), for example rest in the highest place is opposed to rest in the lowest place, and rest in heat is opposed to rest in cold. Rest itself is then classified into three types: natural (طبيعي), forced (قسري), and voluntary (إرادي). Natural rest does not need an external cause; it is based on nature absolutely, because if a body is left alone, it remains in its natural place without seeking to leave it. The author emphasizes that composition (تركب) is not conceivable in rest; only motion can be simple or composite. He then addresses an objection: the rest of a human on the ground seems composite of natural and voluntary. The answer is that it is actually one (natural), and the voluntary aspect is merely the will's act of not removing it (i.e., refraining from moving). The complete cause of rest in each case (natural, voluntary, forced) is only effective when the cause of motion is not predominant. This contrasts with motion, which can admit two causes together because it can have intensity and weakness, as in a stone thrown downward where the natural and forced motions combine not as composition but as intensification (اشتداد).

Key Terms
تضاد السكون
سكون طبيعي
سكون قسري
سكون إرادي
الطبيعة
الإرادة
التركيب
الاشتداد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human rest on the ground is a composite of natural rest and voluntary rest.
Correction: It is a single natural rest; the will merely refrains from moving, not adding a separate cause.

Checkpoint
Why is the rest of a human being on the ground considered natural and not composite?
A) Because the will always causes motion, so rest is always forced.
B) Because the natural tendency is to rest, and the will only removes the intention to move.
C) Because voluntary rest is impossible; all rest is either natural or forced.
D) Because the earth is not a natural place for humans.

Key Takeaway
Rest is simple and opposed by its subject, with three types; it never contains composition, unlike motion which can have intensification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you choose to remain still in a good action, is your rest truly from your own will or from your nature? Are you aware that your will only refrains from moving away from obedience, while the real cause is the natural inclination of your purified soul?
?
The passage says rest is simple, not composite. In your spiritual life, do you seek to combine motives (fear, hope, love) or do you simplify your intention (ikhlas) for Allah? What false compositions have you allowed in your heart's rest?
?
Consider the rest of a stone on the ground: it does not seek to leave its place. Is your heart at rest in its natural place of servitude to Allah, or are you constantly seeking to move away into desires? What is the predominant cause that prevents the motion of sin in your soul?
